# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Summary

I've successfully traced the controller registration process in **kubernetes/kubernetes** and created a comprehensive analysis in `/workspace/answer.json`. Here are the key findings:

### Core Architecture

**1. Controller Interface** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_descriptor.go`)
- All controllers must implement: `Name()` and `Run(context.Context)`
- Defines the standard contract for reconciliation loops

**2. ControllerDescriptor Pattern**
- Registers controllers with metadata and constructors
- `BuildController()` method creates actual controller instances
- Supports feature gates, aliases, and special handling flags

**3. Manager Registration Flow** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`)
- **Run()** - Main entry point orchestrating startup
- **BuildControllers()** - Creates all controllers from descriptors
- **RunControllers()** - Starts each controller in separate goroutines with graceful shutdown

**4. Controller Loop Wrapper** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_utils.go`)
- `controllerLoop` adapts domain-specific controllers to the standard interface
- Separates business logic from manager infrastructure

**5. Concrete Example: Namespace Controller**
- `NewNamespaceController()` - Creates controller with work queue and informer handlers
- `Run(ctx, workers)` - Executes reconciliation loop processing deletions
- Wrapped in manager via `newControllerLoop()` in `core.go`

### Key Files Identified
- Manager infrastructure: `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/`
- Domain controllers: `pkg/controller/`
- Base interfaces: `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/`

The architecture cleanly separates manager lifecycle management from individual controller logic through the Controller interface and descriptor patt

This is only for retry speed and its only the overall factor (not per item)\n114: \t\t&workqueue.TypedBucketRateLimiter[string]{Limiter: rate.NewLimiter(rate.Limit(10), 100)},\n115: \t)\n116: }\n117: \n118: // enqueueNamespace adds an object to the controller work queue\n119: // obj could be an *v1.Namespace, or a DeletionFinalStateUnknown item.\n120: func (nm *NamespaceController) enqueueNamespace(ctx context.Context, obj interface{}) {\n121: \tkey, err := controller.KeyFunc(obj)\n122: \tif err != nil {\n123: \t\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithContext(ctx, err, \"Couldn't get key for object\", \"object\", obj)\n124: \t\treturn\n125: \t}\n126: \n127: \tnamespace := obj.(*v1.Namespace)\n128: \t// don't queue if we aren't deleted\n129: \tif namespace.DeletionTimestamp == nil || namespace.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() {\n130: \t\treturn\n131: \t}\n132: \n133: \t// delay processing namespace events to allow HA api servers to observe namespace deletion,\n134: \t// and HA etcd servers to observe last minute object creations inside the namespace\n135: \tnm.queue.AddAfter(key, namespaceDeletionGracePeriod)\n136: }\n137: \n138: // worker processes the queue of namespace objects.\n139: // Each namespace can be in the queue at most once.\n140: // The system ensures that no two workers can process\n141: // the same namespace at the same time.\n142: func (nm *NamespaceController) worker(ctx context.Context) {\n143: \tworkFunc := func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n144: \t\tkey, quit := nm.queue.Get()\n145: \t\tif quit {\n146: \t\t\treturn true\n147: \t\t}\n148: \t\tdefer nm.queue.Done(key)\n149: \n150: \t\terr := nm.syncNamespaceFromKey(ctx, key)\n151: ",

Manager Registration Flow (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go)\\n\\nThe main entry point **Run()** function (line 185) orchestrates the controller lifecycle:\\n\\n1. **BuildControllers()** (line 256) - Creates all controllers from their descriptors:\\n   - Iterates through all ControllerDescriptors\\n   - Calls BuildController() for each descriptor\\n   - Collects controllers into a slice\\n   - Registers health checkers and debug handlers\\n\\n2. **RunControllers()** (line 271) - Starts all controllers concurrently:\\n   - Launches each controller in a separate goroutine\\n   - Applies jitter to stagger controller startup\\n   - Calls controller.Run(ctx) for each controller (line 722)\\n   - Manages shutdown gracefully with timeouts\\n\\n### 4. Reconciliation loop continues until manager shutdown\\n\\nThis architecture separates domain-specific controller logic (pkg/controller/*) from manager infrastructure (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app), allowing clean composition and lifecycle management of multiple independent controllers within a single process.\"\n}\n",
